NH PBH [Alteration of Gk. nomos (= an\par}{s12 ything allotted or assigned; usage; custom; law), which is related to nemein (=\par}{s12  to deal out, distribute, allot; to allot pasture, pasture, drive to pasture), \par}{s12 from IE base nem- (= to divide, distribute, allot). See נוֹמָד and cp. words th\par}{s12 ere referred to. The change of Gk. nomos to נִימוֹס in Hebrew is due to dissimi\par}{s12 lation. According to a well-known linguistic law of the Hebrew language if o or\par}{s12  u sounds follow each other in two neighboring syllables, the first is generall\par}{s12 y changed into i. cp. e.g. חִיצוֹן (= outer, exterior), which derives from חוּץ\par}{s12  (= out of, outside), and תִּיכוֹן (= middle, central), which comes from תּוֹךְ\par}{s12  (= in the midst of); see חִיצוֹן and תִּיכוֹן. According to my opinion the wor\par}{s12 d נִימוֹס also owes its form to the same law of dissimilation. The change of Gk\par}{s12 . nomos to נִימוֹס is very important because it proves that this law (the law o\par}{s12 f Philippi) continued to be valid during the period of the Mishnah and Talmud, \par}{s12 and was applied even to words of foreign origin. cp.
